It is inspiring to see a family coming together to purchase a home. Hearing them talk about how they plan on coordinati", ...', ng the EMI payments and organizing expenses shows the value that informal sector families place on home ownership, something that is often taken for granted by different sectors of society.   ',  MHFC was started to help families like the Chauhans own a home. Informal sector families are often shunned by commercial banks because of a lack of income documentation - but our experience over the past 8 years has proven that the informal sector is just as, if not more, creditworthy than the traditional salaried sector.  ', u" Under the government's ", #', housingforall', u" scheme, numerous affordable housing projects have sprouted across the country, which is finally meeting the demand from families like the Chauhans. ",  There has never been a better opportunity to help someone you know (domestic staff, employees etc) purchase a home of their own. With a presence in 7 states and a customer base of over 12,000 (and counting), our little company has grown. However, our dedication to the informal sector and focus on affordable housing projects remains as steadfast as ever. ',  This customer from Chittorgarh is perfectly representative of our profile - living in an ancestral home in a joint family of 13 people with no property in his name, he has', ...',  been sanctioned a home loan of Rs. 2 lakhs after putting in a down payment of Rs. 40,000. This amount was paid from his life savings, carefully built over 30 years of operating a fast-food egg stall. His monthly income of Rs. 12,000 is supplemented by his son\u2019s income of Rs. 10,000 from running a poultry shop and together, father and son plan to pay off the loan in about 5 years. ',  We look forward to sanctioning the next Rs. 500 crore as we expand to more states and help more people in the informal sector achieve their dream of home ownership. ',  ', #', informalsector',  ', #', microfinance',  ', #', affordablehousing',  ', #', financialinclusion', Micro Housing Finance Corporation',   ', 27 October 2016',   ', u"Season's Greetings from all of us at MHFC!", Micro Housing Finance Corporation',  shared ', Humans of Bombay', u"'s ", photo', .',   ', 17 October 2016',   ', Humans of Bombay',   ', 17 October 2016',   ', "I've been driving this cab since 35 years now.  I'm old, but I still have to support myself.  Over the years there have been so many experiences -- I've seen t', ...', u"he best and worst of this city.  Sometimes, people like you will talk to me, atleast make me feel human and then there are others who come and scream at me because they're in a hurry and there's too much traffic. ",  A few years ago, at around 12:30 am one night,  I noticed a young girl, not over 25 walking from the bus stop, possibly towards her home.  It was one of those dingy lanes where there aren't a lot of people.  I noticed her, because she looked very anxious and when I looked behind her I saw these 2-3 drunk fellows whistling, and calling her names.  They then began to actively chase her and I was still across the street -- so as a reflex I decided to start honking continuously.  The noise created enough alarm, because they were startled and immediately ran away in the other direction.  I crossed over, and told that girl that I would drop her home -- she was so terrified, she had gone completely pale.  We drove in silence for those 2-3 minutes....her house was just around the corner, but when she stepped outside, she caught both my hands, started weeping and thanked me over and over again.  Even though I said it's okay and that I would have done it for anyone, she insisted that I wait outside while she went in to get something.  She came out with a tin of rasgullas and told me to take them home to my family -- I thanked her and left.  I barely knew her for 10 minutes, but I don't think I'll ever forget that night."',  ', See more', Micro Housing Finance Corporation',   ', 13 October 2016',   ', This enterprising family has a few different sources of income - while our applicant has been running a roadside tempo repair shop for the past 35 years at a monthly income of Rs. 15,000, his wife works as a housemaid while also roasting chanaa at home to be sold to street vendors, earning around Rs. 5000. As they currently live in a kacha house on encroached land, this will enable them to finally have a proper home of their own. ', u" This is a Pune family consisting of the applicant (23 year old) and his parents - all of whom are working. Th", ...', e father is a very experienced tailor with 40 years experience - specialising in stitching military uniforms - photos of his shop attached.',  They currently live in an ancestral kaccha home but with the help of a 11 lakh loan from MHFC, they will be moving into a 1 BHK flat in a formal project soon. It was a tight case for us but given their enterprise and also the fact that they will qualify for a 2.2 lakh subsidy under ', #', PMAY', , we were very happy to support their dream.',  ', #', informalsector',  ', #', housingforall',  ', #', CLSS',  ', #', tailor',  ', #', Pune',  ', #', A1',  ', See more', Micro Housing Finance Corporation',  added ', 2 new photos', .',   ', 6 December 2016',   ', u"Geetaben Chauhan (pictured below) purchases and polishes old utensils throughout the week, after which she sets up a stall at the local Sunday market in Ahmedabad. Her husband and younger son contribute to the family income pool by working as welders on a contractual basis. Her elder son works as a tailor, earning Rs. 9000 per month for making men's shirts.  It is inspiring to see a family coming together to purchase a home. Hearing them talk about how they plan on coordinati", ...', ng the EMI payments and organizing expenses shows the value that informal sector families place on home ownership, something that is often taken for granted by different sectors of society.   ',  MHFC was started to help families like the Chauhans own a home. Informal sector families are often shunned by commercial banks because of a lack of income documentation - but our experience over the past 8 years has proven that the informal sector is just as, if not more, creditworthy than the traditional salaried sector.  ', u" Under the government's ", #', housingforall', u" scheme, numerous affordable housing projects have sprouted across the country, which is finally meeting the demand from families like the Chauhans. The government's loan subsidy program has also helped thousands of families across the country - MHFC alone has helped 1300 customers get subsidies on their home loans.  ",  There has never been a better opportunity to help someone you know (domestic staff, employees etc) purchase a home of their own. All you need to do is refer them to MHFC and we will take it from there.',  ', See more', Micro Housing Finance Corporation',   ', 21 November 2016',   ',   ', MHFC sanctions Rs. 500 Cr worth of home loans', 21 November 2016',  in ', Mumbai, India', This month, MHFC reached a major milestone - Rs. 500 crore worth of sanctions. With a presence in 7 states and a customer base of over 12,000 (and counting), our little company has grown. However, our dedication to the informal sector and focus on affordable housing projects remains as steadfast as ever. ',  This customer from Chittorgarh is perfectly representative of our profile - living in an ancestral home in a joint family of 13 people with no property in his name, he has', ...',  been sanctioned a home loan of Rs. 2 lakhs after putting in a down payment of Rs. 40,000. ",  A few years ago, at around 12:30 am one night,  I noticed a young girl, not over 25 walking from the bus stop, possibly towards her home.  It was one of those dingy lanes where there aren't a lot of people.  I noticed her, because she looked very anxious and when I looked behind her I saw these 2-3 drunk fellows whistling, and calling her names.  They then began to actively chase her and I was still across the street -- so as a reflex I decided to start honking continuously.  The noise created enough alarm, because they were startled and immediately ran away in the other direction.  I crossed over, and told that girl that I would drop her home -- she was so terrified, she had gone completely pale.  We drove in silence for those 2-3 minutes....her house was just around the corner, but when she stepped outside, she caught both my hands, started weeping and thanked me over and over again.  Even though I said it's okay and that I would have done it for anyone, she insisted that I wait outside while she went in to get something.  She came out with a tin of rasgullas and told me to take them home to my family -- I thanked her and left.  I barely knew her for 10 minutes, but I don't think I'll ever forget that night."',  ', See more', Micro Housing Finance Corporation',   ', 13 October 2016',   ', This enterprising family has a few different sources of income - while our applicant has been running a roadside tempo repair shop for the past 35 years at a monthly income of Rs. 15,000, his wife works as a housemaid while also roasting chanaa at home to be sold to street vendors, earning around Rs. 5000.
